## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of population size P and time t. This is a fundamental problem in population ecology where various growth models describe how populations grow, saturate, decline, or oscillate depending on density-dependent and time-dependent factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, low population density)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/microbial growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible inflection point)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized growth curve)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (simplest linear model)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Harvesting/immigration model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (logistic with constant immigration/harvesting)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric scaling of growth rate)
- Delayed logistic approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P * t (time-dependent modification)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating reproduction minus mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Population proportional growth Ôćĺ multiplicative P factor in growth rate (dP/dt ~ P * f(P))
- Carrying capacity / density dependence Ôćĺ polynomial or rational terms in P that change sign at equilibrium (e.g., 1 - P/K)
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) Ôćĺ cubic or quadratic terms creating an unstable lower equilibrium (P*(P-a)*(K-P))
- Multiple equilibria in population models Ôćĺ polynomial expressions in P with multiple real roots
- Metabolic scaling in growth Ôćĺ fractional power laws P**c with c between 0 and 1 (e.g., 2/3 or 3/4)
- Competition or self-limitation Ôćĺ negative quadratic term -c*P^2 representing intraspecific competition
- Logarithmic growth regulation Ôćĺ log(P) terms indicating multiplicative/proportional feedback (Gompertz-type)
- Seasonal or periodic forcing Ôćĺ trigonometric terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) modulating growth parameters
- Extinction dynamics Ôćĺ terms ensuring dP/dt = 0 when P = 0 (biological consistency requires P as a factor)
